- **Subject layer:** `societies/`, `cultures/`, `sites/`, `institutions/`, `phenomena/`
- **Shared:** `comparisons/`, `timelines/`, `queries/`, `sources/`
- **Hubs:** `hubs/theory/`, `hubs/thinkers/`, `hubs/studies/` (portals + `templates/`)
- **Collection:** `raw/` (un-ingested queue), vault-root `Structural_Sources.md`
- **No content pages or sources ingested** — collection is empty; coverage unaudited

---

## [2026-07-08] ingest | Mead: Mind, Self, and Society (Definitive Edition) | social-psychology / sociology / philosophy | classical-era–fieldwork-revolution | [Pages created: 11] | [Pages updated: 1]

Ingested the University of Chicago Press "Definitive Edition" (2015; Morris ed., annotated by Huebner & Joas) of *Mind, Self, and Society* (1934), ~204k words / 20,645 lines / 560 pp., via deployed-subagent strategy: 7 Sonnet extraction agents over disjoint body ranges (front matter, Parts I–IV, Supplementary Essays, Huebner source appendix) writing register-tagged claims files to the scratchpad; all page creation, cross-linking, and voice audit on the main thread. First Chicago-tradition / micro-interactionist source in the wiki.

- **Created (11):** `thinkers/mead-george-herbert`; `disciplines/social-psychology` (subfield of sociology); `theories/social-behaviorism`, `theories/symbolic-interactionism`, `theories/pragmatism`; concepts `significant-symbol`, `gesture`, `taking-the-role-of-the-other`, `generalized-other`, `the-i-and-the-me`, `the-social-self`, `play-and-the-game`; `debates/mind-self-society-authorship-debate`; `sources/mead-mind-self-society-1934`.
- **Updated (1):** `disciplines/sociology` (social-psychology strand, subfield link, theoretical landscape, coverage note).
- **Apparatus:** `index.md`, `overview.md`, `Structural_Sources.md`.
- **Handling flags:** Theoretical/lecture-compilation work — all substantive claims in attributed voice. CRITICAL PROVENANCE: Mead wrote no book; the text is Morris's posthumous compilation from student/stenographic lecture notes (1928 transcript + Page's 1930 notes + fragments, 1912–1931). "Social behaviorism" and the sentence "Our behaviorism is a social behaviorism" are Morris's, not Mead's; the "generalized other" and triadic meaning enter via Page's 1930 notes (Huebner 2015) — captured in the authorship debate. Mead's 1920s human/insect/vertebrate contrasts and child/"primitive man" analogies flagged as dated, attributed. Supplementary Essays (Mead's own MSS) treated as higher-fidelity than the lecture-note main text.
- **Not created (deliberate):** studies/ page; Thinkers-Hub biography (Mead qualifies — future candidate, pre-named `hubs/thinkers/mead-george-herbert`); standalone pages for "biologic individual" and Mead's ethics (folded into thinker page); individualist-vs-social-self debate (deferred pending Cooley ingest).
- **Filed:** source → `raw/sociology/` (line-count 20,645 verified against cache). No PDF deletion (epub→txt source; original .txt filed).
